THOMAS J. GLASER, Chief Financial Officer, Bureau of Finance
I am transm itting for your approval an Ordinance authorizing the execution of an interest rate swap
agreement between Cook County and Lehman Brothers Special Financing, Inc. on the County's l 999A
General Obligation Capital Improvement Bonds.

66

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR SEPTEMBER 5, 2002

PROPOSED ORDINANCE
ORDINANCE Authorizing the Execution and Delivery of
One or More Interest Rate Agreements Relating to the
General Obligation Capital Improvement Bonds, Series
1999A of The County of Cook, Illinois.
Whereas, Section 6(a) of Article VJI of the 1970 Constitution of the State of Illinois provides
that "a County which has a Chief Executive Officer elected by the electors of the County ... (is) a Home
Rule Unit" and The County of Cook, Illinois (the "County"), has a Chief Executive Officer elected by the
electors of the County and is therefore a Home Rule Unit and may, under the power granted by said
Section 6(a) of Article VII of the Constitution of 1970, exercise any power and perfom1 any function
pertaining to its government and affairs, including, but not limited to, the power to tax and to incur debt;
and
Whereas, the County has heretofore issued its General Obligation Capital Improvement Bonds,
Series I 999A (the "Bonds") pursuant to an Ordinance adopted by the Board of Commissioners of the
County on April 6, 1999; and
Whereas, it is in the best interests of the inhabitants of the County and necessary for the
government and affairs of the County to authorize the execution and delivery of one or more interest rate
agreements with respect to the Bonds to, among other things, assist the County in managing its debt
service payments relating thereto; and
Whereas, the County has detern1ined that it is advisable and necessary to authorize the execution
and delivery of one or more interest rate agreements described in Section 2.2 (each, an "Interest Rate
Agreement" and collectively, "Interest Rate Agreements"):
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT ORDAINED BY THE BOARD OF COMMISSIONERS OF
THE COUNTY OF COOK, ILLINOIS, AS FOLLOWS:
ARTICLE I.
Definitions and Interpretations
Section 1.1.
Successors and Assigns. Whenever in this Ordinance the County is named or
referred to, it shall and shall be deemed to include its successors and assigns whether so expressed or not.
All of the covenants, stipulations, obligations, and agreements by or on behalf of, and other provisions for
the benefit of, the County contained in this Ordinance shall bind and inure to the benefit of such
successors and assigns and shall bind and inure to the benefit of any officer, board, commission,
authotity, agent or instrumentality to whom or to which there shall be transfe1Ted by or in accordance with
law any right, power or duty of the County, or of its successors or assigns, the possession of which is
necessary or appropriate in order to comply with any such covenants, stipulations, obligations,
agreements or other provisions of this Ordinance.
Section 1.2.
Parties Interested Herein. Nothing in this Ordinance expressed or implied is
intended or shall be construed to confer upon, or give to, any person or corporation, other than the County
and any counterparty to an Interest Rate Agreement (each, a "Counterparty"), any right, remedy or claim
under or by reason of this Ordinance or any covenant, condition or stipulation thereof. All the covenants,
stipulations, promises and agreements in this Ordinance contained by and on behalf of the County shall be
for the sole and exclusive benefit of the County and any Counterparty.

67

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR SEPTEMBER 5, 2002

Section 1.3.
Severability of Invalid Provisions. If any one or more of the covenants or
agreements provided in this Ordinance on the part of the County to be performed should be contrary to
law, then such covenant or covenants, agreement or agreements, shall be deemed separable from the
remaining covenants and agreements, and shall in no way affect the validity of the other provisions of this
Ordinance.
ARTICLE II.
Determinations and Obligations of the County
Section 2.1.
Authority for Ordinance. The Board of Commissioners hereby finds that all of
the recitals contained in the preambles to this Ordinance are full, true and correct and does hereby
incorporate them into this Ordinance by this reference.
This Ordinance is adopted pursuant to Section 6 of Article VII of the lllinois Constitution of
I 970. The County has ascertained and hereby determines that each and every act, matter, thing or course
of conduct as to which provision is made in this Ordinance is necessary in order to carry out and
effectuate the public purposes of the County.
It is found and determined that the execution and delivery of one or more Interest Rate
Agreements as authorized by this Ordinance are necessary for the welfare of the government and affairs
of the County, are for proper public purposes and are in the public interest.

Section 2.2.
Execution of Interest Rate Agreements. The President of the Board of
Commissioners (the "President") or the Chief Financial Officer of the County (the "Chief Financial
Officer") is hereby authorized to execute and deliver from time to time one or more agreements with
Counterparties selected by the Chief Financial Officer, the purpose of which is to hedge or manage the
County's interest cost with respect to the Bonds (or any portion thereof), or to reduce the County's
exposure to fluctuations in the interest rate or rates payable on the Bonds (or any portion thereof) or to
insure, protect or preserve its investments from any loss (including, without limitation, loss caused by
fluctuations in interest rates, markets or in securities). The stated aggregate notional amount under all
such Interest Rate Agreements authorized hereunder shall not exceed the aggregate principal amount of
the Bonds outstanding (net of offsetting transactions entered into by the County). Any such agreement to
the extent practicable shall be in substantially the fonn of either the Local Currency - Single Jurisdiction
version or the Multicurrency-Cross Border version of the 1992 ISDA Master Agreement accompanied by
the U.S. Municipal Counterparty Schedule published by the International Swaps and Derivatives
Association, Inc. (the "JSDA ") or any additional schedule or successor fonn to be published by the ISDA,
and in the appropriate confirmations of transactions and credit support and security agreements governed
by that agreement, with such insertions, completions and modifications thereof as shall be approved by
the officer of the County executing the same, his or her execution to constitute conclusive evidence of the
Board of Commissioners approval of such insertions, completions and modifications thereof. Amounts
payable by the County under any such agreement shall (i) be a general obligation of the County payable
from any lawfully available funds or (ii) constitute operating expenses of the County payable from any
moneys, revenues, receipts, income, assets or funds of the County available for such purpose, as the Chief
Financial Officer may from time to time detennine. Nothing contained in this Section shall limit or
restrict the authority of the President or the Chief Financial Officer to enter into similar agreements
pursuant to prior or subsequent authorization of the Board of Commissioners.
Section 2.3.
Approval of Financing Team. The selection of the following party or parties in
the capacities as indicated is hereby ratified and approved:

ARTICLE III.
Miscellaneous
Section 3.1.
Authorized Acts. The officers, agents and employees of the County are
authoiized, empowered and directed to do all such acts and things and to execute and deliver all such
documents and certificates as may be necessary to carry out and comply with the provisions of this
Ordinance. All acts and undertakings of the officers of the County that are in conformity with the
purposes and intent of this Ordinance and in furtherance of the execution and delivery of Interest Rate
Agreements authorized hereunder shall be, and the same are, in all respects, approved and confirmed.
Section 3.2.
Enactment. This Ordinance shall constitute full authority for the execution and
delivery of one or more Interest Rate Agreements. All ordinances, resolutions, or orders, or parts thereof,
in conflict herewith, be and the same are hereby expressly repealed.
This Ordinance shall be operative, effective and valid upon its passage by the Board of Commissioners
and its approval by the President.

Commissioner Daley, seconded by Commissioner Lechowicz, moved to suspend the rules so that this
matter may be considered. The motion carried unanimously.
Commissioner Daley, seconded by Commissioner Butler, moved that the Proposed Ordinance be
approved and adopted. Following discussion, Commissioners Daley and Butler withdrew their motion.
Commissioner Daley, seconded by Commissioner Hansen , moved that the Proposed Ordinance be
referred to the Committee on Finance. (Comm. No. 254414). The motion carried unanimously.

ORDINANCE
Transmitting a Communication, dated July 25 , 2002 from
WALLY S. KOS, P.E., Superintendent of Highways
Re:

Speed Limit Zoning Ordinance
Cook DuPage Road,
Plainfield Road and 60th Street
in the Village of Burr Ridge

J respectfully submit to your Honorable Body and recommend for adoption, an ordinance revising the
speed limit on Cook DuPage Road between Plainfield Road and 60th Street which is under the
maintenance jurisdiction of Cook County. The recommended speed limit was detennined by engineering
and traffic investigation in accordance with the provisions of Article VI of the IIJinoi s Vehicle Code and
as more fully explained in the following ordinance.
It is respectfully requested that, should your Honorable Body concur in these recommendations, the
ordinance be adopted.

02-0-26
ORDINANCE
IT IS HEREBY DECLARED, by the Board of Commissioners of Cook County, IIJinois, that the basic
statutory vehicular speed limits established by Section I 1-60 I of the Illinois Vehicle Code are greater, or
less, than that considered reasonable and proper on the road listed below for which the County has
maintenance responsibility and which is not under the jurisdiction of the Deparh11ent of Transportation,
State of Illinois; and

81

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR SEPTEMBER 5, 2002

BE IT FURTHER DECLARED, that this Board has caused to be made an engineering and traffic
investigation upon the road listed below; and
BE IT FURTHER DECLARED, that by virtue of Section I 1-604 of the above Code, this Board
determines and declares that reasonable and proper absolute maximum speed limits upon the roads
described below shall be as stated herein; and
BE IT FURTHER DECLARED, that signs giving notice thereof shall be erected in conformance with the
standards and specifications contained in the Manual on Uniform Traffic Control Devices, the Illinois
Supplement to the National Manual on Unifonn Traffic Control Devices and the Standard Specifications
for Traffic Control Items; and
BE IT FURTHER DECLARED, that this ordinance shall take effect immediately after the erection of said
signs giving notice of the maximum speed limits.
COOK COUNTY HIGHWAY DEPARTMENT

in the Village of Deerfield
Section: 98-A5019-03-EG

87

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR SEPTEMBER 5, 2002
On February 3, 1998, the Cook County Board of Commissioners approved an agreement with the
aforesaid Consultant for engineering services involving the reconstruction of Lake-Cook Road, from the
Tri-State Tollway to Waukegan Road. The County agreed to compensate the firm for such work in the
amount of the fee based on the Time Schedule set forth in the Agreement, $944,001.17. Additionally, the
Section Number of the original contract was amended from 98-A5019-03-RP to 98-A5019-03-EG on July
9, 1998.
It is now necessary for the Consultant to do additional engineering work including new traffic counts,
traffic projections, re-analysis of traffic capacity, lane reduction alternatives studies, right-of-way impact
studies, traffic signal warrant analysis, construction phasing and report revisions. The County will
compensate the Consultant based upon an estimate of costs in a letter to the County, submitted herewith
hereto and amounting to $135,486.94.

02-R-436
RESOLUTION

Resolved, that the President of the Board of Commissioners of Cook County, Illinois, on behalf of the
County of Cook, is hereby authorized and directed by the Members of said Board, to execute, by original
signature or his authorized signature stamp, three (3) copies of a Supplemental Agreement, submitted,
with McDonough Associates, Inc., (hereinafter Consultant) for additional engineering services required in
preparation of studies for County Project Section: 98-A5019-03-EG, Lake-Cook Road from the Tri-State
Tollway to Waukegan Road, said additional services to include new traffic counts, traffic projections,
reanalysis of traffic capacity, studies of lane reduction alternatives, right-of-way impacts, traffic signal
warrant analysis, construction phasing and report revisions; and, said Consultant shall be compensated for
such additional work in the amount not to exceed $ 135,486.94; and, the Highway Department is
authorized and directed to return an executed copy of this Agreement with a Certified copy of this
Resolution to said Consultant.
September 5, 2002

RESOLUTION
WHEREAS, the Cook County Board of Commissioners has the legal authority to authorize its
departments and offices to open and maintain and close imprest cash accounts at various banks; and
WHEREAS, the Cook County Highway Department currently operates the following free checking and
non interest-bearing account with Associated Bank, Chicago, Illinois:
Public Funds Checking Account Number 2169905677; and
WHEREAS, the following are the names of those persons who were authorized to sign checks on this
imprest cash account by a Resolution adopted by the Board of Cook County Commissioners at their
meeting held on June 2, 1998:

2. Marlene Dantino

WHEREAS, effective September 3, 2002, this imprest petty cash account is closed for the following
economical reasons:

2. Minimal account use and check writing
3. Anticipated maintenance fee imposition due to low account balance

deleted.

Transmitting a Communication, dated Jul y 16, 2002 from
WALLY S. KOS, P.E. , Superintendent of Highways
Motor Fuel Tax Project
Appropriating Resolution
Highway Investigations, Studies and Planning
Countywide
Section: 03-6HISP-27-ES
Fiscal Impact : $1 ,900,000.00 from the Motor Fuel Tax Fund (600-600 Account)

89

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR SEPTEMBER 5, 2002

02-R-438
RESOLUTION
APPROPRIATING RESOLUTION

WHEREAS, it is necessary to assure the maximum of services and safety for Cook County Highways in
this area; and

WHEREAS, it is necessary to continually detennine the quality and quantity of services being rendered
by these County Highways; and

WHEREAS, such determination will assure the judicious use of funds available to the County to satisfy
the needs of the general motoring public; and

NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, in accordance with 605 ILCS, Article 5, Division 5, Section
701 .6, 111inois Highway Code, that Motor Fuel Tax Funds be appropriated for the collection of traffic,
soils, inventory and right of way data, conducting surveys, traffic and geometric studies, structure
inspections, drainage studies, program cost estimates and right-of-way studies and the preparation of
reports necessary for determining the annual and long range highway transportation plan, all regarding the
judicious planning for the construction, reconstruction, improvement and maintenance of County
Highways and shall be designated as County Section: 03-6HISP- 27-ES (Highway Investigations,
Studies and Planning - 2003); and

BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that such appropriation will cover the period from December I, 2002 to
November 30, 2003; and

BE lT FURTHER RESOLVED, that such investigations, studies and planning shall be accomplished by
the County through its officers, agents or employees; and

BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that there is hereby appropriated the sum of One Million Nine Hundred
Thousand and No/ I00 Dollars, ($ 1,900,000.00) from the County's allotment of Motor Fuel Tax Funds for
these investigations, studies and planning; and

BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that the Clerk is hereby directed to transmit two (2) certified copies of
this Resolution to the District Office of the Illinois Department of Transportation.
September 5, 2002

Commissioner Carr, seconded by Commissioner Moreno, moved that the Appropriating Resolution be
approved and adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

requesting authorization to accept a grant in the amount of $20,090.00 from the Illinois Attorney
General's Office. This grant is funded through the Violent Crime Victims Assistance Act Program and
supplements the County's current salary for the executive director of the court's Children 's Advocacy
Rooms and the Children's Advocacy Clinic.
The court operates eight (8) Chi ldren's Advocacy Rooms in the following court facilities: the Richard J.
Daley Center, 50 West Washington Street; the Domestic Violence Section of the First Municipal District,
1340 South Michigan Avenue; Juvenile Court, 1100 South Hamilton Avenue; the Expedited Child
Support Center, 32 West Randolph Street; the Family Mediation Unit, Cook County Administration
Building, 69 West Washington Street; the Domestic Relations Court, 28 North Clark Street; the Fourth
Municipal District in west suburban Maywood and the Sixth Municipal District in south suburban
Markham. The Children's Advocacy Clinic operates in the Domestic Violence Courthouse at 1340 South
Michigan A venue.
The authorization to apply for this grant was approved on May 21 , 2002 by the Cook County Board of
Commissioners.
This grant expired at the end of the state's fiscal year on June 30, 2002. No cash matching funds are
required.

30, 2003.

JUVENILE PROBATION DEPARTMENT
CONTRACTS

Transmitting a Communication from
TIMOTHY C. EVANS, Chief Judge, Circuit Court of Cook County
requesting authorization for the Purchasing Agent to enter into a contract with Treatment Alternatives for
Safe Communities (TASC) of Chicago, Illinois, to provide screening, assessment and diagnostic services,
and substance abuse testing for minors in the Juvenile Court Drug Treatment Program.
Reason:

The Circuit Court initiated this unique program in October 1996 for minors with drug-related
offenses who have been identified by the Juvenile Probation and Court Services Department
to be in need of intervention, treatment services, and supervision. The program targets
nonviolent delinquent minors residing in and around the Austin and Lawndale communities in
Chicago. The objective of the program is to provide a continuum of services to these minors
to help break the cycle of drug dependency. Program services include substance abuse
assessment and treatment, health care, counseling, education, vocational training, and housing
placements. Services are provided within a framework of sanctions and substance abuse
testing.

Estimated Fiscal Impact: $74,495.00. Contract period: October I, 2002 through September 30, 2003.
(326-249 Account). Requisition No. 23260032.

106

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR SEPTEMBER 5, 2002

Commissioner Maldonado, seconded by Commissioner Sutker, moved that the County Purchasing Agent
be authori zed to enter into the requested contract. The motion carried unanimously.

*****
Transmitting a Communication from
TIMOTHY C. EVANS, Chief Judge, Circuit Court of Cook County
requesting authorization for the Purchasing Agent to enter into a contract with Aunt Martha' s Youth
Service Center, Inc., Matteson, Illinois, to provide evening reporting center services for girls and boys.
Reason:

Aunt Martha's Youth Service Center, Inc. provides community-based pretrial services for preadjudicated minors charged in delinquency proceedings, 10 to 17 years of age, who are at risk
of being detained in the Juvenile Temporary Detention Center. These services include crisis
intervention, home monitoring, educational advocacy, substance abuse screening and
assessment, recreational services and transportation. Since the inception of the evening
reporting center program in 1995, the court has opened seven alternative detention faci lities,
six for boys and one for girls, and successfully diverting over 9,450 minors from the detention
center. Since that time, 93 percent of the minors who have participated in the program have
not violated the tenns of their probation.

Estimated Fiscal Impact: $1,844,250.00 (Year I: $307,375.00; and Year 2: $ 1,536,875.00). Contract
period: September 30, 2002 through September 29, 2003. (326-249 Account). Requisition No.
23260029.

Commissioner Maldonado, seconded by Commissioner Sutker, moved that the County Purchasing Agent
be authorized to enter into the requested contract. The motion carried unanimously.

DEPARTMENT OF PLANNING AND DEVELOPMENT
HOME INVESTMENT PARTNERSHIPS PROGRAM

Transmitting a Communication, dated August 7, 2002 from
GWENDOLYN D. CLEMONS, Director, Department of Planning and Development
Re:

Home Investment Partnerships Program (HOME Program)
Seguin Services, Inc.

respectfully request approval for the County to enter into twenty-seven (27) subordination agreements
with Seguin Services, Inc. The Cook County Board of Commissioners approved a restructuring of a
series of HOME loans to Seguin Services, Inc. ("Seguin") in relation to the group homes that it operates
for developmentally disabled adults. That restructuring, which reduced the interest rate on these loans
from 3% to I% has been finalized. Seguin Services, Inc. has now submitted a request for the County to
subordinate its loans on twenty-seven (27) of these properties to new senior loans. This request is part of
Seguin Services, Inc. 's continued effort to restructure its debt and improve its cash flow.

108

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR SEPTEMBER 5, 2002

I respectfully request approval of this subordination request and that the Chief Administrative Officer of
the County of Cook or his designee, be authorized to execute on behalf of the County of Cook, twentyseven (27) subordination agreements, as well as any closing related documents required by this title
company.

of the Department of Planning and Development be approved. The motion carried unanimously.

Transmitting a Communication, dated August 8, 2002 from
DENNIS MANZKE, Chief of the Administrative Services Bureau, State's Attorney' s Office
requesting authorization to apply for a new grant in accordance with Section 29 of the 2002 Cook County
Budget Resolution. This grant, in the amount of $400,000.00 from the Illinois Criminal Justice
Infonnation Authority (ICJIA), will provide funding for the Victim Assistance Services to the
Underserved Populations Program. This program consists of a total of five (5) victim specialists who will
be assigned to the Victim Witness Assistance Program and includes two (2) Spanish-speaking specialists,
two (2) Polish-speaking specialists and one ( 1) traffic court specialist. This grant requires that the office
match 25% of the grant award. The match commitment for this program is an in-kind match that funds
the salary and fringe benefits of one of the Spanish-speaking specialists.

30, 2004.

DENNIS MANZKE, Chief of the Administrative Services Bureau, State' s Attorney's Office
requesting authorization to accept a grant in the amount of $1 I ,025.00 from the Illinois Attorney
General's Office. This grant provides continued funding for our Hidden Victims Support Group Program
that consists of three (3) monthly support groups provided by the State' s Attorney 's Victim Witness
Assistance Program for survivors of homicide victims: one (I) for adolescents ages 13 through 18 years
of age and two (2) for adults, one ( 1) of which is located in Oak Park and the other one (I) in Markham.
These groups are facilitated by a licensed clinical social worker, along with a representative of the Victim
Witness Assistance Program and provide early and ongoing intervention emotional support and group
therapy to the families/survivors of homicide victims. This program has been funded annually since 1985
by the Illinois Attorney General's Office.

Commissioners.

furniture and equipment to include the following manufacturers: KMI/Lincora, Inwood, Tyco, Tract, and
OSI.
These companies can provide furniture and equipment that is compatible with existing furniture currently
within the Office. The increase in funds is due to a reassessment of current needs within the office.
One time purchase. (*717/060-530 and 534-530 Accounts). Requisition Nos. 20600013 and 25340001.
*Sufficient funds have been appropriated to cover this request.
Commissioner Maldonado, seconded by Commissioner Sutker, moved that the request of the Chief
Financial Officer of the Treasurer's Office be approved. The motion carried.
Commissioner Moran voted "present".

to accept Proposed Settlement of $30,000.00 for the release and settlement of suit regarding
Sabich v. Velasco, Case No. 99-L-11405. This matter involves a claim by the plaintiff
alleging injury in a traffic accident which occurred in October 1998. The matter has been
settled for the sum of $30,000.00, which is within the authority granted to this office by the
Finance Committee's Subcommittee on Litigation at its meeting of June 1 I, 2002. State's
Attorney recommends payment of $30,000.00, made payable to George Sabich and his
attorneys, Serpico & Novelle, Ltd. Please forward the check to Robert F. Cleary, Assistant
State' s Attorney, for transmittal.

Sheriff s Police Officer. The matter has been settled for the sum of $20,000.00, which is

the Comptroller in accordance with the attached report prepared by the Department of Risk
Management, Workers' Compensation Unit. Reimbursement by the Forest Preserve District
financial department will be made to the County Comptroller on a monthly basis. This
request covers bills received and processed from August 2 through September 5, 2002.

COMMISSIONER SILVESTRI, SECONDED BY COMMISSIONER GOSLIN, MOVED
APPROVAL OF THE EMPLOYEES' INJURY COMPENSATION CLAIMS. THE MOTION
CARRIED.

CLERK OF THE CIRCUIT COURT, Dorothy Brown, transmitting a Communication:

POLITANO, Tinley Park, Illinois, to assist in the implementation of effective records
management practices. Specifically, he will develop the specifications for the upgrade and/or
replacement of existing micrographics equipment, perform a needs assessment for an imaging
system, and recommend operational metrics.
Reason:

James Politano is a Certified Document and Imaging Architect (CDIA+) and has
extensive experience in business process improvement for document
management, image management and records management systems.

2003. (529-260 Account). Requisition No. 25291394.

REPORT OF THE COMMITTEE ON FINANCE (BID AWARDS)
September 5, 2002
The Honorable,
The Board of Commissioners of Cook County

ATTENDANCE
Present:

Chairman Daley, Vice Chainnan Carr, Commissioners Butler, Goslin, Hansen, Lechowicz,
Maldonado, Moran, Moreno, Quigley, Schumann, Silvestri, Sims, Steele and Sutker ( 15)

Absent:

Commissioner Collins and President Stroger (2)

Ladies and Gentlemen:
Your Committee on Finance, having had under consideration the matters hereinafter mentioned,
respectfully reports and recommends as follows:

264

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR SEPTEMBER 5, 2002

SECTION 1
Your Committee has considered the bids submitted on the items hereinafter described in accordance with
the specifications on file in the Office of the County Purchasing Agent.
Communications from the County Purchasing Agent submitting recommendations on the award of
contracts or quotations for said items, be and upon adoption of this Report awarded as follows.
The deposit checks are ordered returned to the unsuccessful bidders at once and to the successful bidders
upon the signing of the contract or quotation.

AN ORDINANCE AMENDING CHAPTER 10:

steeply; and

region's capacity, will close by the end of the year 2000; and

239003

TO DIRECT COOK COUNTY TO DEVELOP AND IMPLEMENT A PLAN TO REDUCE
COUNTY WASTE THROUGH REUSE AND RECYCLING (PROPOSED ORDINANCE).
Submitting a Proposed Ordinance sponsored by John H. Stroger, Jr., President, Allan C. Carr,
Mike Quigley, John P. Daley, Gregg Goslin, Carl R. Hansen, Joseph Mario Moreno, Roberto
Maldonado, Herbert T. Schumann, Jr., Peter N. Silvestri, Deborah Sims, Bobbie L. Steele and
Calvin R. Sutker, County Commissioners:

273

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR SEPTEMBER 5, 2002

PROPOSED ORDINANCE
WHEREAS, Cook County recently evidenced its commitment to recycling by passing an
ordinance mandating the purchase of recycled products; and
WH EREAS, recycling saves energy and natural resources, and reduces the use of toxic
chemicals in the manufacturing process; and
WHEREAS, recycling at a 25% diversion rate would reduce the County's waste d isposal
costs by 25%; and
WHEREAS, waste disposal is an enormous expense for municipal governments, costing the
City of Chicago alone $31.2 million; and
WHEREAS, seven landfills in the Chicago Metropolitan Area, representing 21 % of the
region 's capacity, will close by the end of the year 2000, raising the cost of waste disposal
still further; and
WH EREAS, the success of recycling programs depends on "closing the loop": collecting
recyclable products to create a supply of material, remanufacturing products, and purchas ing
recycled products to create a market; and
WHEREAS, the Illinois Department of Commerce and Community Affairs reports that 600
firms are engaged in the business of recycling in Illinois; and
WHEREAS, Cook County can save money while reducing waste by reducing its use of
materials and reusing materials where feasible;
NOW THEREFORE BE IT ORDAINED, that Cook County develop and implement a plan to
reduce and reuse material, and to recycle material from all County facilities; and
BE IT FURTHER ORDAINED, that such plan be calculated for the purpose of achieving a
county-wide goal of 25% waste diversion and an accompanying 25% waste disposal cost
reduction.

*Referred to the Environmental Control Committee on 10-04-00.
Commissioner Quigley, seconded by Commissioner Schumann, moved to accept the Substitute
Ordinance for Communication No. 239003. The motion carried.

SUBSTITUTE ORDINANCE FOR COMMUNICATION No. 239003
AN ORDINANCE TO DIRECT COOK COUNTY TO DEVELOP AND IMPLEMENT
A PLAN TO REDUCE COUNTY WASTE THROUGH REUSE AND RECYCLING
WHEREAS, Cook County reeeRtly evidenced its commitment to recycling by passing an ordinance
mandating the purchase of recycled products; and
WHEREAS, recycling saves energy and natural resources, prevents the emission of many greenhouse
gases, and reduces the use of toxic chemicals in the manufacturing process; and

274

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR SEPTEMBER 5, 2002

WHEREAS, recycling at a 25% diversion rate would reduce the County's waste disposal costs by 25%;
and
WHEREAS, waste disposal is an enormous expense for municipal governments, costing the City of
Chicago alone~ .$..l21 million; and
WHEREAS, the Illinois Environmental Protection Agency reports that the landfill capacity of the
Chicago Metropolitan Area has only seven years remaining, and the subsequent higher transportation
expenses will raise se"'eA landfills iA the Chisago Metropolitan Area, representing 21% of the region' s
eapaeity, will elose ey the e0EI of the year 2QOO, raisi0g the cost of waste disposal still further; and
WHEREAS, the success of recycl ing programs depends on "closing the loop": collecting recyclable
products to create a supply of material, remanufacturing products, and purchasing recycled products to
create a market; and
WHEREAS, the Illinois Department of Commerce and Community Affairs reports that ~2,400 finns,
employing 56,000 people, are engaged in the business of recycling in Illinois; and
WHEREAS, Cook County can save money while reducing waste by reducing its use of material s and
reusing materials where feasible;
NOW THEREFORE BE IT RESOLVED, that Cook County develop and implement a plan to reduce
and reuse material, and to recycle material from all County facilities; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that such plan be calculated for the purpose of achieving a countywide goal of 25% waste diversion and an accompanying 25% waste disposal cost reduction.
Louis DeRose, Acting Director, Cook County Department of Environmental Control, stated that within
the last 5 years, the Cook County Board of Commissioners, the Environmental Control Committee and
the Department of Environmental Control have addressed the issues of recycling and waste management.
The Cook County Board of Commissioners adopted the Cook County Solid Waste Management Plan that
sets forth requirements for recycling and also the adoption of a Solid Waste Coordinator. Regarding the
proposed ordinance at hand, the Cook County Department of Environmental Control supports the
proposal.
Louis DeRose asked Raymond Akers, Solid Waste Coordinator, to provide infonnation and insight
regarding county recycling and waste management. He further commented that the Sheriffs Office
oversees certain waste recycling programs for the county.
Raymond Akers commented that one year ago he, Commi ssioner Quig ley and the Sheriffs Custodi al
Office met to discuss recycling and waste management. Since then a major study has been undertaken of
the court facilities. It has been proposed that compactors be installed as it was detennined that over 50%
of the Sheriff s facilities' waste was paper and cardboard . The study resulted in the recommendation that
the present cost could be reduced by separating cardboard, mixed paper and office paper. If this
recommendation proves successful , the Sheriffs Custodial Department will expand the plan to include
county facilities such as the hospitals. He said there is a bid opening scheduled for September IO, 2002.

275

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR SEPTEMBER 5, 2002
Commissioner Quigley stated that he had met with fonner Environmental Control Director Charles
Lagges and Michael Finn, who determined that because there are several elected officials, different
haulers, and different facilities, all under the rubric of Cook County, the county should establish a unified
plan. Also, employees need to be both educated and given the opportunity to recycle. Cook County
should be a leader among counties by meeting the Illinois goal of recycling 25% of all waste.
Commissioner Hansen inquired whether the proposed ordinance applied to only Cook County
government and not to any municipalities or unincorporated areas.
Chairman Moreno replied that the ordinance applied only to Cook County government.
Commissioner Hansen inquired what the net cost and impact on the County budget would be. He
commented that certain municipalities make a profit on their recycling. He also contrasted the problems
that Chicago is having with the blue bag program against the fact that the Mt. Prospect residential
community recycles 60% of its waste.
Louis DeRose replied that, as with the vast majority of waste management projects, he recommends that a
cost/benefit analysis be undertaken. Mistakes can occur, as in DuPage County, were the solid waste
recycling program turned out to be too much of a taxpayer burden. In contrast, there is the Illinois
ordinance controlling air pollution that resulted from an ozone study, where the legislature placed a
premium on the benefit.
Chairman Moreno pointed out that the last paragraph of the proposed ordinance recommended that a plan
be developed for the purpose of further reviewing cost.
Commissioner Silvestri stated that certain government responsibilities should not be looked at as revenue
sources, and perhaps inherently require investment, such as schools, the CTA and recycling. He stressed
that the environment needs to be protected as a place we live in, not to preserve its pristine beauty. He
pointed out the problematic nature of a cost/benefit analysis to certain situations. Commissioner Silvestri
asserted that certain issues are just matters of doing the right thing, and that this is the right thing because
an inherent responsibility of government is not just to constituents but to our children and grandchildren.
Commissioner Quigley inquired what the tipping fee is at the dump for waste hauled away from the
County.
Raymond Akers responded that waste goes to a transfer station on the South Side and that the tipping cost
is between $30 and $35 per ton.
Commissioner Quigley noted that studies show that waste removal costs go down when paper recycling is
implemented. He inquired whether this was Mr. Akers' impression.
Raymond Akers responded that this was correct, that the study on their facilities indicates that garbage
collection drops in cost by well over 50% with paper and cardboard recycling.
Commissioner Quigley stated that, in speaking with the City of Chicago's Department of the
Environment, he understood that they had a request for proposal for the recycling of high quality paper
for which they were paid a nominal amount. It also saved the City waste hauling expense. The
commissioner asked if a substantial amount of the county's waste in this building is paper and cardboard?
Louis DeRose responded that paper was at least, conservatively, 50%.

276

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR SEPTEMBER 5, 2002

Commissioner Quigley noted that the household is the most expensive entity to recycle from, given the
complexity of recyclables.
Louis DeRose confinned this, adding that it is by far the most expensive, and that what the County Board
is dealing with in its facilities is mainly paper goods. He stated that the reason he brought up the DuPage
example was to illustrate that it is imperative to do a cost/benefit analysis. Man hours need to be looked
at, there needs to be a procedure and a hard financial number. There seems to be general agreement that
the financial situation most likely would range somewhere between a slight cost to possibly a profit.
Commissioner Quigley stated that the other half of this building (the City of Chicago) recycles and they
do not lose money.
Commissioner Hansen stated that the Board needs to know the financial impact of the ordinance, whether
positive or negative, before approving it. He also stated that the market for recyclables is tenuous. For
example a number of governments have stopped recycling newspaper because there is no market for it.
He stated that the Board might want to do adopt the ordinance regardless of cost because the ordinance is
a good idea; it is, however, responsible to know what to budget and what impact the ordinance will have
on taxpayers. Also the Board should pick and choose the recyclables according to cost-paper is any easy
choice, but the Industrial Engineers operation should take a look at the situation and prepare some figures
for the Board.
Raymond Akers stated that the market looks to be coming back at the moment. Quoting from the
Chicago transacted paper stock values from August I 0, 2002 they read: mixed paper $40-$45 per ton,
newspapers $65-$70 per ton, old corrugated cardboard $95-$100 per ton , and sorted white ledgers $130$ 140 per ton.
Commissioner Butler noted that when he convenes the bid openings, recycled paper is considerably more
expensive than regular paper. He asked why that is.
Commissioner Quigley responded that because the Board passed a purchasing ordinance and other
governmental bodies, there was a great cost differential given to recycled paper to encourage the market.
It worked, because there was a lot of recycled paper available. The cost of recycled paper is now on a par
with regular paper. Nationally there is a glut of recycled paper and the markets are growing. Per the
county ordinance, all of the Board's copy paper is recycled and almost all other paper is recycled. The
exception is chlorine-free paper; where there is a big cost difference. Commissioner Quigley stated that
the Board ' s hope is that the chlorine paper market will expand as well. Other elected officials are
following suit, such as the Treasurer's Office. He concluded by stating that the Purchasi ng Agent has
done a great job in moving the Board toward purchasing recycled paper.
Commissioner Butler requested that the ordinance plan include a cost history of what the Board has paid
for virgin and recycled paper over the past four years.
Commissioner Quigley stated the plan should also include the cost history Commissioner Butler
requested, a cost analysis of recycling various waste products, taking into account the offsetting savings
in waste disposal, and a societal analysis.
Chainnan Moreno stated that it is the intent of the language to develop and implement a plan to include a
cost benefit analysis.

Commissioner Quigley, seconded by Commissioner Silvestri, moved approval of the Substitute
Ordinance (Communication No. 239003). The motion carried.

241446

AN ORDINANCE DIRECTING COOK COUNTY TO ADOPT LEADERSHIP IN
ENERGY AND ENVIRONMENTAL DESIGN (LEED) GREEN BUILDING RATING
SYSTEM FOR ALL NEWLY CONSTRUCTED COUNTY FACILITIES (PROPOSED
ORDINANCE). Submitting a Proposed Ordinance sponsored by Mike Quigley, County
Commissioner; Co-Sponsored by William R. Moran and Herbert T. Schumann, County
Commissioners:
The following is a synopsis of the Proposed Ordinance:
PROPOSED ORDINANCE
WHEREAS, the United States Green Building Council (USGBC), a non-profit, nationally
recognized association with membership representing all segments of the building
industry, including architects, manufacturers, government agencies, and environmentalists,
has created LEED, a green building rating system that provides specific principles and
practices, some mandatory but the majority discretionary, that may be applied during the
design, construction, and operation phases, which enable the building to be awarded points
from reaching preset standards of environmental efficiency so that it may achieve LEED
certification from the USGBC as a "green" building; and
THEREFORE BE IT RESOLVED,

I.
That Cook County does hereby order all of its newly constructed
buildings to employ the LEED Green Building Rating System, Version 2.0, throughout
their design, construction, and operation and does further order that each new building
must achieve the LEED silver level of certification.
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED,
II.
That the USG BC intends to release a revised version of the LEED Green
Building Rating System every three years; and with this in consideration when beginning a
new building project, Cook County shall refer to the most current version of the LEED in
existence; and after registering with the USGBC at the design stage of the project as is
required, the County may adhere to that existing version until completion of the project,
regardless of any new LEED version that may be released at a later time.
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED,
III.
That with specific regard to the LEED Energy and Atmosphere category,
because achieving increasing levels of energy performance above the set energy code
standards is the surest way of realizing significant operational cost savings, all buildings
must obtain a total of at least eight points.

279

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDfNGS FOR SEPTEMBER 5, 2002

BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED,
IV.
That Cook County also encourages the application of LEED principles
during retrofit and renovation projects of its current standing structures whenever it is
practicable.
NOTE:

This matter was also referred to the Committee on Construction. (See Comm.
No. 24 1445).

* Referred to the Environmental Control Committee on 02-06-01.
Commissioner Quigley, seconded by Commissioner Sims, moved to defer Communication No.
241446. The motion carried.
244064

POLLUTION FROM COAL-FIRED POWER PLANTS (PROPOSED RESOLUTION).
Submitting a Proposed Resolution sponsored by William R. Moran, County Commissioner.
Co-sponsored by Peter N. Silvestri, County Commissioner.
PROPOSED RESOLUTION
WHEREAS, air pollution has been shown to be a contributing factor to premature death,
aggravating asthma and is especially harmful to vulnerable groups such as children, the
elderly and people with existing lung and heart disease; and
WHEREAS, the United States Environmental Protection Agency has ruled that the
Chicago metropolitan area is a severe non-attainment area for ozone and failure to conform
with the U.S. Environmental Protection Agency Clean Air Act standards; and
WHEREAS, non-attainment area status could lead to a loss of federal transportation
dollars, the curtailment of economic opportunities and the imposition of other federal
sanctions that could erode local control for the Chicago metropolitan area; and
WHEREAS, the twenty-five coal-fired power plants in Illinois are a significant source of
air pollution in Illinois, emitting smog-fonning nitrogen oxides, sulfur dioxide contributing
to particulate poll ution and carbon dioxide contributing to climate change and toxic metals;
and
WHEREAS , the coal-fired power plants of Illinois were built between 1951 and 1975
making them exempt from meeting the pollution standards of the Clean Air Act; and
WHEREAS, pollution from coal-fired power plants could be reduced by installing modem
pollution controls or burning cleaner fuels such as natural gas; and
WHEREAS, there is a threat to the health and safety of the residents of Cook County and
the State of Illinois because of the emissions from the coal-fired power plants.
NOW, THEREFORE BE IT RESOLVED, by the Cook County Board of
Commissioners that the Board does hereby urge Governor George Ryan and the Illinois
General Assembly to ensure that pollution from coal-fired power plants be dramatically
reduced by passing legislation that would effectively end the "grandfathering" of these
plants from the new plant emission standards of the Clean Air Act;

280

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR SEPTEMBER 5, 2002

BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED that a suitable copy of this Resolution be presented to
Governor George Ryan and the Illinois General Assembly.

* Referred to the Environmental Control Committee on 06-05-01.
Commissioner Moran, seconded by Commissioner Quigley, moved to defer Communication No.
244064. The motion carried.

245584

ENCOURAGING PACE TO CONTINUE TO TRANSPORT QUALIFIED INDIVIDUALS
UNDER THE AMERICANS WITH DISABILITIES ACT (PROPOSED RESOLUTION).
Submitting a Proposed Resolution sponsored by William R. Moran, Coun ty Commissioner:
PROPOSED RESOLUTION

WHEREAS, Mass transit is most important to individuals who can not provide their own
transportation; and
WHEREAS, Pace and many other transportation organizations are trying to control spending
in order to lower their spending in order to pay the increase costs of fuel; and
WHEREAS, one proposal involves eliminating bus routes and other services in order to save
money; and

WHEREAS, eliminating routes will leave some individuals wi th no transportation to and
from their jobs; and
WHEREAS, in several meetings regarding changes in routes the people affected have
pleaded for the route to continue and even offered to pay increased fa res to increase the funds
of the transportation provider; and
WHEREAS, Pace is considering the elimination of a route they have provided for
individuals working at the LARC (Lansing Association of Retarded Citizens) facility in
Lansing, Illinois; and
WHEREAS, by eliminating this service Pace has provided for LARC, the families of the
individuals going there, and many of the individuals will have no other way to go to the
LARC facility in order to work; and
WHEREAS, the United States Department of Transportation regulations require
transportation providers to transport qualified individuals under the Americans with
Disabilities Act within :X to I Yi a mile of transportation routes, leaving some Americans with
no transportation options if they go beyond this covered area; and

284

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR SEPTEMBER 5, 2002

WHEREAS, the State of Illinois requires downstate transportation authorities to maintain a
profit of twelve percent, yet Chicago area transportation providers must maintain a forty
percent profit, creating a greater financial burden on Cook County residents and
transportation providers; and
WHEREAS, all the levels of government and the transportation providers should work
together in order to assure that those who most need mass transit are able to get to and from
their destinations.
NOW, THEREFORE BE IT RESOLVED, the Cook County Board of Commissioners
encourages Pace to continue to transport qualified individuals under the Americans with
Disability Act, and others who can not transport themselves, to and from their destinations in
and around Cook County; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that transportation providers should pay special attention
to areas which contain people unable to provide their own transportation when creating,
maintaining, altering or discontinuing any transportation routes; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, the Cook County Board of Commissioners does hereby
encourage the Federal and State of Illinois Governments to examine the transportation issues
mentioned within this Resolution, especially services for qualified individuals under the
Americans with Disabilities Act and the amount of profit required for transportation
providers.
Commissioner Moran, seconded by Commissioner Schumann, moved to receive and file
Communication No. 245584. The motion carried.
Commissioner Schumann moved to adjourn the meeting, seconded by Commissioner Moran. The
motion carried and the meeting was adjourned.
Respectfully submitted,
COMMITTEE ON LEGISLATION AND INTERGOVERNMENTAL RELATIONS
CARL R. HANSEN, Chainnan
ATTEST: SANDRA K. WILLIAMS, Secretary

ORDINANCE

02-0-28
ORDINANCE
Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE JOSEPH MARIO MORENO, ROBERTO MALDONADO,
JOHN P. DALEY AND PRESIDENT JOHN H. STROGER, JR.
COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
Co-Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE JERRY BUTLER, ALLAN C. CARR, GREGG GOSLIN,
CARL R. HANSEN, TED LECHOWICZ, WILLIAM R. MORAN, MIKE QUIGLEY,
HERBERT T. SCHUMANN, JR., PETER N. SILVESTRI, DEBORAH SIMS,
BOBBIE L. STEELE AND CALVIN R. SUTKER, COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
WHEREAS, the County of Cook is a home rule unit of government pursuant to the Illinois Constitution
ofl970;and
WHEREAS, pursuant to its home rule power, the Board of Commissioners of Cook County may exercise
any power and perfonn any function relating to its government and affairs including protecting the public
health, welfare and safety of its citizens; and
WHEREAS, many Mexican immigrants are fearful of reporting crimes to the police because they do not
possess proper identification; and
WHEREAS, many Mexican immigrants have difficulty conducting daily routine business transactions,
including check cashing, credit card purchases, driver's license application, and store layaway purchases,
among other things, because they do not possess proper identification; and
WHEREAS, in 46 cities across the United Sates, including Chicago, the Mexican Consulate issues
identification cards entitled "matricula consular" to Mexican nationals with a birth certificate and proper
photo identification who have been residing in the United States for at least six months; and
WHEREAS, the Board of Commissioners of Cook County wishes to enable Mexican immigrants to
utilize the " matric ula consular" as legal identification when interacting with County departments.
NOW, THEREFORE BE IT ORDAINED BY THE BOARD OF COMMISSIONERS OF COOK
COUNTY:
Section I: Chapter 5, Departments and Agencies, of the Cook County Ordinances is hereby amended by
the addition of the following new Section 5-4 as follows:

286

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR SEPTEMBER 5, 2002

5-4. Recognition of Matricula Consular as valid identification. When requiring members of
the public to provide identification, each County department shall accept as valid
ide ntification of the person a " matricula consular" identification card issued by the Mexican
Consulate. The requirements of this section do not apply under circumstances where ( l) a
federal or state statute, administrative regulation or directive, or court decision requires the
County to obtain different identification, (2) a federal or state statute or administrative
regulation or directive preempts local regulation of identification requirements, or (3) the
County would be unable to comply wi th a condition imposed by a funding source, which
would cause the County to lose funds from that source.
Nothing in this section is intended to prohibit the County department from ( I ) asking for additional
infonnation from individuals in order to verify a current address or other facts that would enable the
department to fulfi ll its responsibilities, except that this section does not pennit the department to require
additional information solely because the Matricula Consular is the fonn of identification presented, (2)
using fingerprints for identification purposes under circumstances where the department also requires
fingerprints from persons who have a driver's license or State identification card.
Section 2: This ordinance shall take effect immediately upon approval.

Commissioner Moreno, seconded by Commissioner Maldonado, moved that the Ordinance be approved
and adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

Sponsored by

COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
WHERE AS, Almighty God in His infinite wisdom has called from our midst REVEREND ALVIN F.
HARRIS, JR., born into time on February 24, 1946, and born into eternity on July, 29, 2002, and
WHEREAS, Reverend Harri s, affectionately known as "Butch'', was born to the union of Alvin and
Dorothy Harris in Chicago, Illinois, and was the eldest of their children, and
WHEREAS, Reverend Harris attended the John D. Shoop Elementary School where he graduated, and
went on to attend Morgan Park High School in Chicago, Illinois, and

287

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR SEPTEMBER 5, 2002

WHEREAS, Reverend Harris grew-up in the community of Morgan Park. He accepted Christ and was
baptized at an early age at the Mt. Joy Missionary Baptist Church in Chicago, Illinois, where his
grandfather, who he loved and honored, was a Deacon. Under the leadership of the late Reverend lvory
Scott, Reverend Harris faithfully attended Sunday School and sang in the choir, and
WHEREAS, Reverend Harris was groomed by his grandfather, and became a young man with strong
morals and values, and
WHEREAS, Reverend Harris, at the age of 12, was a helper on the truck for "Flashback Cleaners". As a
teen, he was mentored by Hank Black and was taught all the facets of the carpeting business. Later, he
began to work for Conrail Railroad Company, where he remained for 20 years. While there, he was a
shop steward for two years for the Transport Workers Union, Local 2014 and later became a VicePresident, and
WHEREAS, Reverend Harris was an entrepreneur at the age of twenty-two. He and his brother-in-law
opened their own carpet business, H & B Carpet, which is still successful to this day, and
WHEREAS, Reverend Harris worked at the Cook County State' s Attorney' s Office, and
WHEREAS, Reverend Harris met and married his first love, Lorraine Turner in 1964. To this union,
five children were born: Linda, Frank, Alvin, Jeannine and Ronnie, and
WHEREAS, Reverend Harris in July 1975, met Lorraine Day who became the "apple of his eye". They
were married on July 1985, and remained together until his untimely death. They had five children:
Tanille, Allen, Aaron, Adam and Tiarra, and
WHEREAS, Reverend Harris was appointed Deacon at the Mt. Joy Missionary Baptist Church. In 1987,
Reverend Harris became a part of the St. John Missionary Baptist Church, where Pastor A. Edward Davis,
Jr. appointed him to the Deacon Board where he served faithfully for five years, and
WHEREAS, Reverend Harris in 1992, accepted his calling to the Gospel Ministry and served humbly as
an Associate Minister. He preached his first message, entitled, 'Returning Home". Two months later, he
was offered the Assistant Pastorship at the Straightway Missionary Baptist Church, and
WHEREAS, Reverend Harris was ordained by Pastor A. Edward Davis in 1997. After God called him,
Reverend Harris, subsequently, founded the Christ Total Deliverance Church at 9255 South Cottage
Grove in Chicago, Illinois, from a building, which he purchased and also made into a men's shelter and a
new and used furniture store, called Real Deal, and
WHEREAS, Reverend Harri s later established "The Potter's House", as a refuge for men who had been
forgotten, and
WHEREAS, Reverend Harris was a part of various community organizations. He was the President of
the South End Business and Planning Association. He was President of the 34th Ward Minister's
Alliance, a Member of the PTA of Morgan High School, a Member of the Morgan Park Roots
Committee, Owner of H & B Carpet, founder of the Prophecy Hour Radio Broadcast Ministry on WSSDFM Radio, a Member of the Minister' s Conference, and a Liaison for the Chicago Park District Minister' s
Conference and the Chicago Area Gospel Announcers Guild of the GMW A, Inc., and
WHEREAS, Reverend Harris was preceded in death by his father, Alvin Frank Harris, Sr. and his
youngest brother, Benjamin Harris, and

288

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR SEPTEMBER 5, 2002

WHEREAS, he leaves to cherish fond memories: his wife, Lorraine Day Harris; a loving mother,
Dorothy Harris; ten children: Linda, Frank, Alvin (Rose), Ronnie, Jeannine, Tanille Walker (Demond),
Allen, Aaron, Adam and Tiarra; nine grandsons and four granddaughters; one brother, Ronald Harris; five
sisters: Darlene Bailey, Bunna Thomas (Charles), Janet Goodwin (Joseph), Janice Banks (Clarence) and

WHEREAS, on September 11 , 200 I, terrorists hijacked four civilian aircraft, crashing two of them into
the towers of the World Trade Center in New York City, and a third into the Pentagon outside
Washington D.C.; and

289

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR SEPTEMBER 5, 2002

WHEREAS, the fourth hijacked aircraft crashed in southwestern Pennsylvania after passengers tried to
take control of the aircraft in order to prevent the hijackers from crashing the aircraft into an important
symbol of democracy and freedom; and

WHEREAS, these attacks were by far the deadliest terrorist attacks ever launched against the United
States; and

WHEREAS, in the aftermath of the attacks the people of the United States stood united in providing
support for those in need; and

WHEREAS, the United States Congress, on December 18, 200 I, resolved that September 11th is Patriot
Day; and

WHEREAS, Congress called on State and local governments to observe Patriot Day with appropriate
activities; and

WHEREAS, the Flag of the United States of America will be lowered to half staff on Patriot Day in
honor of the thousands of people who lost their lives as a result of the terrorist attacks against the United
States that occurred on September 11 , 200 l ; and

WHEREAS, Congress called on all of the people of the United States to observe a moment of silence on
Patriot Day in honor of the individuals who lost their lives as a result of the terrorist attacks against the
United States that occurred on September 11 , 2001.

NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Cook County Board of Commissioners joins the
United States Congress and declares September 11 , 2002 Patriot Day and requests that the people of Cook
County honor those killed and injured by the terrorist attacks of September 11, 200 I by flying the flag of
the United States of America, observing a moment of silence and any other tributes.

Approved and adopted this 5th day of September 2002.

02-R-452
RESOLUTION
Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE WILLIAM R. MORAN AND
PRESIDENT JOHN H. STROGER, JR., COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
Co-Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE JERRY BUTLER, ALLAN C. CARR, EARLEAN COLLINS,
JOHN P. DALEY, GREGG GOSLIN, CARL R. HANSEN, TED LECHOWICZ,
ROBERTO MALDONADO, JOSEPH MARIO MORENO, MIKE QUIGLEY,
HERBERT T. SCHUMANN, JR., PETER N. SILVESTRI, DEBORAH SIMS,
BOBBIE L. STEELE AND CALVIN R. SUTKER, COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
WHEREAS, throughout our nation's history, the men and women of America's armed forces have
preserved our freedom, protected our security, and upheld our democratic values; and
WHEREAS, from the battles of the American Revolution through the crucible of two world wars to the
challeng ing peacekeeping and humanitarian missions of today's post cold war era, our men and women in
uni fonn have stood proudly in defense of the United States and the cause of liberty; and
WHEREAS, in the two centuries since our nation's birth, more than a million servicemen and women
have paid the price of that liberty with their lives; and
WHEREAS, joining the ranks of these heroes are the thousands who have been held as prisoners of war
or whose fate has not yet been resolved; and
WHEREAS, many have been lost in the chaos of battle, and the grief of their loss made more acute for
their families and fellow Americans because of the inability to detem1ine whether they perished or
survived; and
WHEREAS, captive Americans, cruelly stripped of their freedom, treated with contempt and brutality, or
used as pawns by their captors in a larger political struggle, have fo ught long, lonely battles against
despair, physical and psychological torture, and the ultimate fear of being forgo tten; and
WHEREAS, Americans will never forget those who have home the indignities and sufferings of
captivity in service to our country, those missing in action, or those who died as prisoners of war, far from
their home and family; and
WHEREAS, on National POW/MIA Recognition Day, we affinn our commitment to those still missing
and renew our pledge to make every effort to obtain the answers to their fate; and
WHEREAS, we can do no less for these American heroes and for their families, who have endured such
profound loss, and whose suffering continues as long as their loved ones' fate remains unknown.

29 1

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR SEPTEMBER 5, 2002
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the President and the Board of Commissioners of Cook
County do hereby recognize September 20, 2002 as POW/MIA Recognition Day and affirm the nation' s
commitment to those still missing; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED , that a suitable copy of this Resolution be presented to the Veteran
Organizations located within Cook County.
Approved and adopted this 5th day of September 2002.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners

adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

RESOLUTION
WHEREAS, we the Cook County Board of Commissioners, as the duly elected body governing Cook
County, have received and reviewed the 200 1 Comprehensive Economic Development Strategy and the
Resolution of the Cook County Economic Development Advisory Committee; and
WHEREAS, we have found the CEDS to fulfil l its function to report on the previous year's economic
activities and effectiveness, to identify changes and trends in the region's economic conditions, and to
present the economic development goals and activities for the coming year; and
WHEREAS, the CEDS meets the requirements of the Economic Development Administration (EDA) to
qualify Cook County, Chicago and suburban jurisdictions within its boundaries as eligible to apply for
EDA funding of economic development projects.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Cook County Board of Commissioners does hereby
approve this 2001 annual report CEDS for submittal to EDA.

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR SEPTEMBER 5, 2002

WHEREAS, the County Board has learned with sorrow of the untimely death of Lee J. Schwartz;
and
WHEREAS, Mr. Schwartz, a graduate of Columbia University and the Harvard Law School , was
a lawyer and gentleman of impeccable honor and reputation; and
WHEREAS, Mr. Schwartz was engaged in the practice of law for over 35 years and was an
expert on legislative matters, municipal law and the Illinois Constitution; and
WHEREAS, Mr. Schwartz served as a Legislative Staff Intern in the Illinois House of
Representatives, was counsel to, inter alia, the Honorable John P. Touhy, Speaker of the Illinois House;
Thomas Arthur "Art" McGloon, Minority Leader of the lllinois Senate; and to three Mayors of the City of
Chicago: the Honorable Richard J. Daley, the Honorable Michael Bilandic, and the Honorable Harold
Washington; and
WHEREAS, while serving on the staff of the Illinois House of Representatives, Mr. Schwartz
worked with, inter alia, then Representative Thaddeus S. Lechowicz; and
WHEREAS, Mr. Schwartz mentored and taught the skills of legislating to young staffers like
David A. Epstein, who became Parliamentarian of the Illinois House and later served as special counsel to
this Board; and
WHEREAS, Mr. Schwartz practiced law for many years with the firm of Sidley & Austin (now
Sidley Austin Brown & Wood), and went on to open his own private law practice, in which he was
known throughout Cook County and Illinois as a tireless advocate of the consumer and taxpayer in
difficult, complex litigation; and
WHEREAS, Mr. Schwartz will be remembered for his devotion to the law, his belief in j ustice,
his legislative expertise, and his fine legal skills; and
WHEREAS, Mr. Schwartz leaves to cherish his memory his wife, Nancy; his sons, David and
Alexander; his sister, Joan; his brother, Gary, and countless friends and colleagues; and
WHEREAS, Lee J. Schwartz will be greatly missed by all who knew him.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Board of Commissioners of Cook County
does hereby express its deep sorrow at the death of Lee J. Schwartz, offers its heartfelt sympathy to his
family in their hour of sorrow and loneliness, for their loss is shared by all Members of this Body and the
people of the County of Cook, and joins his family and friends in honoring his memory; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that a suitable copy of this Resolution be tendered to the family
of Lee J. Schwartz as a memorial of his good works and also spread upon the official proceeding of this
Honorable Body.
Approved and adopted this 5th day of September 2002.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DA YID ORR, County Clerk

Jesse Brown
Passed into eternity August 15, 2002
WHEREAS, Jesse Brown passed from this earth after a long illness; and
WHEREAS, Jesse Brown was born in Detroit, Michigan and grew up on the south side of Chicago,
Illinois; and
WHEREAS, Jesse Brown graduated with honors from Chicago City Colleges and later attended
Roosevelt University in Chicago and the Catholic University in Washington, D.C.; and
WHEREAS, Jesse Brown enlisted in the Marines in 1968; and
WHEREAS, in 1970, Jesse Brown was shot by a sniper while patrolling the DaNang area in Vietnam;
and
WHEREAS, the sniper's shot left Jesse Brown's right arm partially paralyzed; and
WHEREAS, Jesse Brown became involved with the Disabled American Veterans organization; and

298

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR SEPTEMBER 5, 2002

WHEREAS, Jesse Brown began as a supervisor of the national appeals office and rose to deputy national
service director and in 1988 to executive director; and
WHEREAS, Jesse Brown was appointed by President Bill Clinton as Secretary for Veterans Affairs in
1993, a position he held until July 1997.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the President of the Cook County Board and the Board
of Commissioners offers its deepest condolences to the family of Jesse Brown; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that a suitable copy of this Resolution be tendered to the family of
Jesse Brown, that his memory be so honored and ever cherished.

02-R-458
RESOLUTION
Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE JOHN P. DALEY, PRESIDENT JOHN H. STROGER, JR.
AND TED LECHOWICZ, COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
Co-Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE JERRY BUTLER, ALLAN C. CARR, EARLEAN COLLINS,

HERBERT T. SCHUMANN, JR., PETER N. SILVESTRI, DEBORAH SIMS,
BOBBIE L. STEELE AND CALVIN R. SUTKER, COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
WHEREAS this month marks .the eleventh anni versary of a celebration which began in September of
1991 as a day set aside to commemorate the anniversary of the 1963 Civil Rights March on Washington,
D.C., and
WHEREAS this one day event grew to one week of events, and has since become a month-long
celebration that promotes respect for diversity and encourages positive interaction, and
WHEREAS "Strengthening Our City of Neighbors" is the theme for Unity Month 2002, and

299

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR SEPTEMBER 5, 2002

WHEREAS Unity Month is a time to rise above such potentially divisive markers as race, ethnicity,
gender, religion, sexual orientation, and disability, and
WHEREAS understanding and appreciating human differences are key to ensuring a viable future for our
city, and
WHEREAS Cook County has many groups and organizations working to bring people together through
activities in which they share their cultures and experiences, and
WHEREAS during September 2002 the City of Chicago Commission on Human Relations will sponsor
"Unity Month" by holding activities, in partnership with other organizations, to promote exchanges across
racial, ethnic and religious lines, and
WHEREAS the citizens of Cook County have committed themselves to working together to create a
bias-free environment and achieve justice and equal opportunity for all, and
WHEREAS during " Unity Month", people who are not usually placed in situations of cooperation with
one another will be asked to join together in meaningful interaction during organized programs and
activities throughout Cook County, now therefore
BE IT RESOLVED by the Board of Commissioners of Cook County, that September 2002 shall be
designated as "Unity Month" in Chicago, and all to whom these presents may come are invited to
participate in the activities planned for this time, and to work together to promote a civil and democratic
society.

Approved and adopted this 5th day of September 2002.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DAYID ORR, County Clerk

adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

WHEREAS, Almighty God in His infinite wisdom has called from our midst,
ROWLAND A. GLENN
WHEREAS, Rowland A. Glenn was the beloved husband fo r fifty-four years of Janice, devoted father
of Michael, Laurie and (the late) Fredrick, cherished grandfather of Daniel, and dear brother of Shirley
and Armand, and
WHEREAS, Rowland A. Glenn grew up in Albany Park and graduated from Von Steuben High School.
After the war he attended John Marshall Law School. Mr. Glenn devoted his life to his family, his
profession and improving the lives of children, and
WHEREAS, Rowland A. Glenn served his country, enlisting in the Mari nes duri ng World War II. He
taught classes in U.S. and world history while stationed in the Pacific, and
WHEREAS, Rowland A. Glenn became president of the National Association of Women and
C hild ren's Apparel Salesmen in the late 1960s. He started his career as a salesman for his mother-inlaw's dress manufacturing business, Fashions by Helene. Mr. Glenn later became a national sales leader
and head of the Midwest Division of Robby Len Swimwear for forty-one years. He helped the company
develop into a major swimwear line. For sixteen years he was president of Style Exhibitors, a regional
fashion sales association, and
WHEREAS, after his retirement in 1993, Rowland A. Glenn generously volunteered his time weekly for
six years as a tutor in the Cabrini-Green housing development as part of the Working in the Schools
program. His warm, magnetic personality garnered him considerable popularity and success with his
second, thi rd and fou rth grade students. Mr. Glenn's tales of his extensive travels brought geography
alive to his pupils, and
WHEREAS, Rowland A. Glenn further demonstrated his tireless commitment to youth and his
community when he lectured eighth graders for the Executive Service Corps for seven years. He
volunteered at No11hwestem Memorial Hospital for eight years and also worked as a docent at the
Chicago Historical Society, and
WHEREAS, Rowland A. Glenn signed on with a talent agency after his retirement and won bit parts
and was an extra in commercials and movies such as Home Alone, Ali, My Best Friend 's Wedding and
Soul Food. He had a passion for travel that he shared with his wife and together they visited more than
one hundred countries and six continents, and
WHEREAS, Rowland A. Glenn was a devoted fam ily man who believed that fam ily came first. When
his second son succumbed to a rare bone cancer at age sixteen, the family establi shed a cancer research
scholarship at the Weizmann Institute of Science in Rehovoth, Israel, and
WHEREAS, Rowland A. Glenn possessed an indomitable spirit and passion for li fe and left a lasting
legacy of dedication, detennination and commitment to his family, his faith and his community.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Board of Commissioners of Cook County does
hereby express its deep sorrow at the death of Rowland A. Glenn, and offers its heartfelt sympathy to his
family in their hour of sorrow and joins his family in honoring his memory, and

301

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR SEPTEMBER 5, 2002
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that a suitable copy of this Resolution be tendered to the family of
Rowland A. Glenn as a memorial of his good works and spread upon the official proceedings of this
Honorable Body.

WHEREAS, David L. G. Jacobs was born in Chicago and raised in what is now Skokie. He received
his bachelor's degree in economics from DePaul University and a master's degree in economics from the
University of Missouri. Mr. Jacobs was a devoted famil y man and an expert in the fields of business
management and labor relations, and

302

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR SEPTEMBER 5, 2002

WHEREAS, David L. G. Jacobs' skill and success in his field led to work as an independent arbitrator

WHEREAS, Almighty God in His infinite wisdom has called from our midst,
BERNARD G. POLLACK
WHEREAS, Bernard G. Pollack was the beloved husband of Mary Jane, dear father of Jeanie, James
and Daniel, loving stepfather of Thomas, Harry and Barbara, fond grandfather of sixteen, and fond
brother of Billie and Marge, and
WHEREAS, Bernard G. Pollack grew up in Lakeview and graduated from Senn High School. He
attended the University of Wisconsin at Madison on a basketball scholarship and lettered in basketball,
football and track each of the four years he attended, graduating in 1933. Mr. Pollack was a Chicago
legend and business icon known for his tremendous civic-mindedness and philanthropy, and
WHEREAS, Bernard G. Pollack built the Stockyards Packing Company into one of the nation's most
prominent meatpacking businesses . After college he joined the company founded by his grandfather in
1895. Mr. Pollack served as president in the early 1980s and remained there until he retired and sold the
company in 1998. The business supplied some of the best restaurants in the country, and
WHEREAS, Bernard G. Pollack had an extraordinary impact on Chicago's tourism industry. He was
president of the Chicago Convention and Tourism Bureau in 1980 and 198 1, and assiduously promoted
the City of Chicago on behalf of the Bureau for many years, and
WHEREAS, Bernard G. Pollack worked compassionately with the Hundred Club of Cook County, a
civic group that provides financial assistance to families of police officers, firefighters and paramedics
who die in the line of duty. A member since 1970 and a board member since 1987, he found great
satisfaction in contacting the families personally, and
WHEREAS, Bernard G. Pollack generously and tirelessly volunteered his time for the welfare of
others. Along with his wife, he established the Bernard and Mary Jane Pollack Foundation to support
charities. Mr. Pollack organized golf outings to benefit the American Cancer Society and was active in
the Jewish United Fund, and

304

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR SEPTEMBER 5, 2002

WHEREAS, Bernard G. Pollack was an avid golfer and a member of the Evans Scholar Foundation and
a founding member of the Briarwood Country Club in Deerfield. He became a member of Bryn Mawr
Country Club and of Boca Rio Golf Club in Boca Raton, Florida, where he had a winter home. Mr.
Pollack had a natural curiosity and was an enthusiastic reader and traveler studying the language of any
country he would visit, and
WHEREAS, Bernard G. Pollack was a caring humanitarian who made significant contributions to
society and left a lasting legacy of devotion to his family and outstanding leadership and commitment to
his community.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Board of Commissioners of Cook County does
hereby express its deep sorrow at the death of Bernard G. Pollack and offers its heartfelt sympathy to his
family in their hour of sorrow and joins his family in honoring his memory, and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that a suitable copy of this Resolution be tendered to the fami ly of
Bernard G. Pollack as a memorial of his good works and spread upon the official proceedings of this
Honorable Body.
Approved and adopted this 5th day of September 2002.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DAYID ORR, County Clerk

Commissioner Daley, seconded by Commissioner Sutker, moved that the Resolution be approved and
adopted. The motion carried unanimously.
