RESOLUTION
Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE TED LECHOWICZ, PRESIDENT JOHN H. STROGER, JR.
AND JOHN P. DALEY, COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
Co-Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE JERRY BUTLER, ALLAN C. CARR, EARLEAN COLLINS,
GREGG GOSLIN, CARL R. HANSEN, ROBERTO MALDONADO,
WILLIAM R. MORAN, JOSEPH MARIO MORENO, MIKE QUIGLEY,
HERBERT T. SCHUMANN, JR., PETER N. SILVESTRI, DEBORAH SIMS,
BOBBIE L. STEELE AND CALVIN R. SUTKER, COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
WHEREAS, the County Board has learned with sorrow of the death of Zaven 0. Kodjayan, a
long-time successful restauranteur in the City of Chicago; and

305

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR SEPTEMBER 5, 2002

WHEREAS, Mr. Kodjayan came to Chicago in 1968 from Paris, where he had been working at
the George V. Hotel; and
WHEREAS, in the late 1960s and early 1970s Mr. Kodjayan ran the Flame Restaurant in Oak
Brook and the Flame East (later known as the Four Torches) in Chicago; and
WHEREAS, in 1975 Mr. Kodjayan opened Zaven's at 260 East Chestnut Street in Chicago,
which he ran for 27 years until selling earlier this year for health reasons; and
WHEREAS, Mr. Kodjayan was a fixture in the Chicago restaurant community; and
WHEREAS, Mr. Kodjayan was fluent in ten languages and was an accomplished opera singer;
and
WHEREAS, Mr. Kodjayan contributed his time, efforts, and support unselfishly for many years
on behalf of many worthwhile causes, including Special Children 's Charities and the Zaven Kodjayan
Scholarship Foundation, which he started to help young people achieve their dreams of a college
education; and
WHEREAS, Mr. Kodjayan leaves to cherish his memory his wife, Rhonda; his daughters, Nicole
and Dina; his mother, Sima; his brothers, Hagop and Kamig, and many other family members and
friends; and
WHEREAS, Zaven Kodjayan will be missed by all who knew him.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Board of Commissioners of Cook County
does hereby express its deep sorrow at the death of Zaven Kodjayan, offers its heartfelt sympathy to his
family in their hour of sorrow and loneliness, for their loss is shared by all members of this Body and the
people of the County of Cook, and joins his family and friends in honoring his memory; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that a suitable copy of this Resolution be tendered to the family
of Zaven Kodjayan as a memorial of his good works and also spread upon the official proceedings of this
Honorable Body.
Approved and adopted this 5th day of September 2002.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DAYID ORR, County Clerk

adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

02-R-464
RESOLUTION
Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE JOSEPH MARIO MORENO, COUNTY COMMISSIONER
Co-Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE JOHN H. STROGER, JR., PRESIDENT, JERRY BUTLER,
ALLAN C. CARR, JOHN P. DALEY, GREGG GOSLIN, CARL R. HANSEN,
TED LECHOWICZ, ROBERTO MALDONADO, WILLIAM R. MORAN,
MIKE QUIGLEY, HERBERT T. SCHUMANN, JR., PETER N. SILVESTRI,
DEBORAH SIMS, BOBBIE L. STEELE AND CALVIN R. SUTKER
COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
PROCLAIMING SEPTEMBER 12TH TO BE
MEXICAN INDEPENDENCE DAY IN COOK COUNTY

WHEREAS, National Hispanic Heritage Month is a celebration of Hispanic pride and culture,
recognizing the achievements of Hispanic individuals who by hard work and sacrifice have distinguished
themselves through their careers and public service; and
WHEREAS, National Hispanic Heritage Month, created by Public Law 90-498, approved September 17,
1968, by the 90th Congress, authorizing the President to issue annually a proclamation calling upon the
people of the United States to observe such week with appropriate ceremonies and activities; and
WHEREAS, the Act was amended in 1988 by the 1OOth Congress to authorize the designation of National
Hispanic Heritage Month as the 31-day period beginning September 15 and ending on October 15; and
WHEREAS, over 70% of Hispanics living in Cook County are of Mexican decent; and
WHEREAS, on September 15, 1810, the people of Mexico valiantly responded to Father Miguel Hidalgo
y Costilla' s call for independence; and

308

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDfNGS FOR SEPTEMBER 5, 2002

WHEREAS, the courage and sacrifice for freedom demonstrated by Father Hidalgo and other freedom
fighters has been an inspiration to all Mexicans and people throughout the world; and
WHEREAS, in the spirit of Father Hidalgo and other freedom fighters, the Mexican-American
community has fought for social justice throughout Cook County and the United States; and
WHEREAS, Cook County' s Mexican-American community has made numerous cultural and economic
contributions to the growth and development of our county; and
WHEREAS, since its founding in 1969, the Mexican Civic Society has enabled the Mexican-American
community to preserve and transmit its culture to the citizens of Illinois through a variety of activities
throughout the year, including an annual parade, banquet and civic ceremony commemorating Mexico's
independence; and
WHEREAS, Carlos Manuel Sada, Consul General of Mexico, is the official representative to the Midwest
Region of the United States.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Cook County Board of Commissioners, on behalf of
the more than fi ve million residents of Cook County, does hereby proclaim September 12, 2002, to be
MEXICAN fNDEPENDENCE DAY fN COOK COUNTY, in recognition of the contributions the
Mexican community has made throughout the County of Cook, and urge all Cook County residents to
join in this celebration of their culture and heritage; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that a suitable copy of this Resolution be presented to Carlos Manuel
Sada, Consul General of Mexico.

Commissioner Moreno, seconded by Commissioner Butler, moved to suspend the rules so that this matter
may be considered. The motion carried unanimously.
Commissioner Moreno, seconded by Commissioner Maldonado, moved that the Resolution be approved
and adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

ADJOURNMENT
Commissioner Carr, seconded by Commissioner Sutker, moved that the meeting do now adjourn to meet
again at the same time and same place on Thursday, September 19, 2002, in accordance with County
Board Resolution 02-R-08.
The motion prevailed and the meeting stood adjourned.
